Defining Time: The Continuity of Flux and Non-Stability
Author defines time as continuous flux and denies its stability, then addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of time as the continuity of flux and renewal (non-stability), the clarification that 'continuity' is not literal, and how the objection that non-stability is not a quantity is resolved by showing priority and posteriority are inherent to time's parts.

Core Idea
Time is not a static line; its essence is non-stability and continuous flux.

This passage presents a dense definition of time from the Islamic theological tradition. The author defines time as 'the continuity of flux and renewal,' immediately clarifying that 'continuity' here does not mean a static connection. An objection is raised that non-stability cannot be a quantity, and the answer reveals the unique nature of time as a quantity with inherent priority and posteriority. This lesson unpacks these ideas step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and key terms
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Focus on the phrase 'اتصال التصرم والتجدد' and the comment that it means 'عدم الاستقرار' (non-stability). Notice that the author says time is what is prior by essence.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Understand the clarification of 'continuity'
The commentator explains that 'continuity' here does not mean a static connection, because continuity (as a concept) is not a quantity, but time is a quantity. Instead, 'continuity' refers to the continuous nature of time itself—its essential property of being non-stable.
The phrase 'اتصال التصرم' is an exaggeration to emphasize that the necessary property is like the essence.
3
Examine the objection
The objection states that non-stability is a non-existence, and non-existence cannot be a quantity, so time's essence cannot be non-stability. Also, the continuity of non-existence is not a quantity.
This challenges the definition directly.
4
Understand the resolution
The answer is that priority and posteriority are inherent to time's parts by themselves, not by addition of anything else. This makes time a quantity with an intrinsic order. The phrase 'continuity of flux' is an exaggeration to show that this ordering is essential.
This resolves the objection and completes the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا بد من الانتهاء إلى ما تقدمه بالذات، وهو الذي تسميه الزمان ) فإن ماهيته كما ستعرفها اتصال التصرم والتجدد أعني عدم الاستقرار فإذا فرض فيها أجزاء عرض لها [؟] المذكوران لذاتها. قوله: (اتصال) التصرم (والتجدد لم يرد معناه الظاهر، إذ لا يمكن الاتصال والتجدد، ولأن الاتصال ليس كماً والزمان كم بل أراد بالاتصال المتصل فإنهم يعبرون عما هو متصل في ذاته بالاتصال، لكونه لازماً ذاتياً له فكأنه نفس الاتصال وإضافته إلى التصرم والتجدد وجوديته محالين كما هو الظاهر من المتن، أو باستلزامه التسلسل المحال هاهنا وباستلزامه محالاً لا بيان استحالة استلزام التسلسل لما ذكر من المحال حتى يرد ما ذكر تأمل. قوله : ( فإن ما هيته كما ستعرفها اتصال التصرم والتجدد أعني عدم الاستقرار أورد عليه أنَّ ماهية الزمان ليس عدم الاستقرار ولا اتصال ذلك العدم إذ الزمان معدود من أقسام الكم ولا قائل بأن عدم شيء من الأشياء استقراراً كان أو غيره ولا اتصال ذلك العدم من الكم بل له ماهية. فالتقدم والتأخر المذكوران لذاتها، ولا يحتاج في عروضهما لها إلى أمر سواها بخلاف ما عداها فإنه محتاج في عروضهما له إلى أجزاء الزمان ولذلك ينقطع السؤال وجه التقدم إذا انتهى إلى أجزاء الزمان كما مرت إليه الإشارة وقد أجيب عنه أيضاً، بأن إضافة المعروض إلى العارض أي المتصل المتصرم والمتجدد، وإنما اختار هذه المبالغة يجعل لازم الماهية نفس الماهية ليظهر لحوق التقدم والتأخر لأجزائه لذاته أكمل ظهور . قوله : ( أعني عدم الاستقرار) يعني أنَّ المراد بالتصرم والتجدد عدم الاستقرار إذ الامتداد المتصل في ذاته غير متصف بالتصرم والتجدد ما لم يلاحظ انقسامه، بل بعدم الاستقرار فالمعنى حقيقة الزمان المتصل الغير المستقر لذاته كأنه نفس اتصال التصرم والتجدد.
Therefore it is necessary to end with what is prior by essence, and that is what you call time. For its essence, as you will know, is the continuity of flux and renewal, i.e., non-stability. So if parts are supposed in it, the mentioned priority and posteriority are accidental to them by themselves. (Commentator's words:) (Continuity) of flux (and renewal: its apparent meaning is not intended, for continuity and renewal are impossible, and because continuity is not a quantity while time is a quantity; rather by continuity he meant the continuous, for they express what is continuous in itself as continuity, because it is an essential necessary property of it, as if it is continuity itself; and its attribution to flux and renewal ... His saying: (For its essence, as you will know, is the continuity of flux and renewal, i.e. non-stability): it was objected that the essence of time is not non-stability nor the continuity of that non-existence, for time is counted among the divisions of quantity, and no one says that non-existence of something, whether stability or otherwise, nor the continuity of that non-existence, is a quantity; rather it has an essence. Then the mentioned priority and posteriority are by themselves, and they do not need in their occurrence to them anything else, unlike other things which need in their occurrence to them the parts of time; therefore the question of priority is cut off when it ends with the parts of time, as has been indicated. And it was also answered by adding the subject to the accident, i.e. the continuous flux and renewal; he only chose this exaggeration to make the necessary property of the essence the essence itself, to show more fully the attachment of priority and posteriority to its parts by themselves. His saying: (i.e. non-stability) means that by flux and renewal is meant non-stability, for continuous extension in itself is not characterized by flux and renewal unless its division is considered, but rather by non-stability; so the meaning is: the reality of time is the continuous non-stable in itself, as if it is the very continuity of flux and renewal.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage defines time and explains its essence. The text states that time is what is prior by essence, and its essence is the continuity of flux and renewal (ittiṣāl al-taṣarrum wa al-tajaddud), meaning non-stability (ʻadam al-istiqrār). If parts are supposed in time, priority and posteriority belong to them by themselves. The commentator clarifies that 'continuity' here is not literal—time is a continuous quantity, but its continuity is not like a static line; rather it is inherently non-stable. An objection is raised that non-stability cannot be a quantity, but the answer is that priority and posteriority are inherent to time's parts, not due to an external factor. The commentator explains that the author used the phrase 'continuity of flux' as an exaggeration to emphasize that the necessary property (priority/posteriority) is as if it were the essence itself. Finally, 'non-stability' clarifies that time has no fixed state; its reality is a continuous non-stable existence.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That time is a static container or a stable quantity.
Correction: Time's essence is non-stability and continuous flux; it is not static.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the essence of time?
A) A static quantity
B) The continuity of flux and renewal, i.e. non-stability
C) The duration of motion
D) The number of motions

Key Takeaway
Time is a quantity whose essence is non-stability and continuous flux, with priority and posteriority inherent to its parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time's essence is non-stability, then every moment you live is already gone before you can grasp it. How does this change your awareness of the present moment? Will you consciously seize the fleeting seconds before they vanish?
?
The passage says priority and posteriority are inherent to time's parts. Your life is a sequence of these 'parts'. Are you living as if each part is independent, or are you connected by the purpose that gives your life direction? What must change today?
?
Time is a quantity with intrinsic order—you cannot pause it or reorder its parts. This means your past actions are fixed and your future is unfolding. Are you using this unyielding order to build what matters, or are you passively swept along? What will you do with the next hour?

6 min
Time Defined as Continuous Unstable Extension
The author defines time as continuous unstable extension and explains its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic philosophers define time as a continuous entity that is inherently unstable, and how this definition avoids treating time as a discrete quantity.

Core Idea
Time is a continuous extension that is unstable by nature.

This passage delves into the precise definition of time, clarifying that it is not a static continuum but an inherently unstable continuous extension. The author distinguishes between the external reality of time and its mental divisions, ensuring we don't mistakenly treat it as a collection of discrete parts.

Guided Path
1
Understand key terms
Familiarize yourself with 'discreteness' (التصرم), 'renewing' (التجدد), and 'instability' (عدم الاستقرار). The passage equates discreteness and renewing with instability.
2
Grasp the core definition
Time is defined as a continuous extension that is inherently unstable. It is as if time itself is the connection of discreteness and renewing.
Notice that continuous extension alone is not time until instability is added.
3
Examine the argument about priority and posteriority
The author argues that time is not actually characterized by priority and posteriority in the external world. If it were, it would become a discrete quantity with parts existing together.
Priority and posteriority are relations, so their relata must coexist, implying simultaneity.
4
Appreciate the mental nature of temporal parts
When we mentally divide time, the assumed parts acquire priority and posteriority intrinsically because they belong to an unstable continuum.
This shows that time's instability is fundamental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( أعني عدم الاستقرار) يعني أنَّ المراد بالتصرم والتجدد عدم الاستقرار إذ الامتداد المتصل في ذاته غير متصف بالتصرم والتجدد ما لم يلاحظ انقسامه، بل بعدم الاستقرار فالمعنى حقيقة الزمان المتصل الغير المستقر لذاته كأنه نفس اتصال التصرم والتجدد. قوله : ( فإذا فرض إلخ) يعني أنَّه ليس موصوفاً بالتقدم والتأخر في الخارج حتى يلزم كونه كماً منفصلاً وكونه مجتمع الأجزاء، بناء على أن التقدم والتأخر لكونهما إضافتين توجدان معاً فيكون معووضاهما موجودين معاً بل هو أمر متصل في ذاته غير مستقر إذا فرض له أجزاء عرض لها في الذهن التقدم والتأخر لذاتها لكونها أجزاء لأمر غير مستقر .
His saying: (I mean instability) means that what is meant by discreteness and renewing is instability. For the continuous extension in itself is not characterized by discreteness and renewing unless its division is considered; rather, by instability. So the meaning is: the reality of time is the continuous, unstable in itself, as if it were the very connection of discreteness and renewing. His saying: (For if it is assumed, etc.) means that it is not described as having priority and posteriority in the external world, such that it would be a discrete quantity and composed of parts simultaneously, based on the fact that priority and posteriority, being relations, exist together, so their relata would exist together. Rather, it is something continuous in itself, unstable. If parts are assumed for it, then priority and posteriority occur to them mentally by themselves, because they are parts of something unstable.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of time and clarifies its nature. The author comments on the phrase 'I mean instability': what is meant by 'discreteness' (al-tasarrum) and 'renewing' (al-tajaddud) is instability ('adam al-istiqrār). A continuous extension in itself does not exhibit discreteness or renewing unless one considers its division; but time is essentially unstable. Hence, the reality of time is that it is a continuous entity that is inherently unstable, as if it were the very connection of discreteness and renewing. Then, commenting on the phrase 'for if it is assumed' (fā-in furiḍa), the author explains that time is not actually described as having priority and posteriority in the external world, which would imply it is a discrete quantity with parts existing simultaneously. Rather, priority and posteriority are relations that would coexist if their relata existed together. Time itself is a continuous, unstable thing. If one mentally assumes parts of time, then these parts acquire priority and posteriority intrinsically because they are parts of an unstable entity.

Key Terms
عدم الاستقرار
التصرم
التجدد
الامتداد المتصل
كم منفصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is a stable, static continuum.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that time is inherently unstable (غير مستقر), not a static continuum. Its essence involves discreteness and renewing.

Checkpoint
What is the 'reality of time' according to this passage?
A) A discrete quantity
B) A continuous, unstable extension
C) A stable duration
D) A measure of motion

Key Takeaway
Time is a continuous, inherently unstable extension, and its mental parts have relational attributes of priority and posteriority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You experience time as a flow of moments, but this lesson says time is actually a continuous unstable extension, and our mental division into past, present, and future is artificial. How often do you live as if the present moment is fixed and stable, ignoring its constant renewal? What would change if you truly internalized that every instant is new and slipping away? Commit to one specific practice today that reminds you of this instability (e.g., a dhikr or a pause before speaking).
?
The author argues that priority and posteriority are mental relations, not external realities. Do you treat your past as something that actually exists 'back there' and your future as something waiting ahead? How does this belief affect your attachment to past mistakes or anxiety about the future? Name one past event you cling to; how can you reconnect its instability as a mental construct and free yourself from its hold?
?
If time is inherently unstable, then your very existence is a continuous renewal. Are you living as if you are the same person you were a moment ago? What would it mean to embrace that you are, in every new moment, a new creation from Allah? Write one intention for the next hour that acknowledges this fresh start.

beginner

Imaginary Movement Is Purely Imaginary
Argument that imaginary movement is externally unreal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mutakallimun's argument that imaginary movement cannot have external existence because it is attributed to pure non-existents.

Core Idea
What is attributed to non-existents cannot be externally real.

This lesson examines the first part of the mutakallimun's reasoning about time and movement. The author begins by asserting that what we call 'imaginary movement' is indeed imaginary, not real. He gives a proof based on the fact that possibilities of duration are attributed to things that no longer exist, like the time between historical events. This establishes that such movement cannot be externally existent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the literal meaning.
Notice the author's use of examples from prophetic history.
2
Identify the core argument
The passage argues that imaginary movement is imaginary because an existent cannot subsist in an imaginary thing. Also, the fact that possibilities of increase and decrease are attributed to pure non-existents proves they are not externally real.
The example of durations between prophets illustrates the second point.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: If something can be ascribed to non-existents, how can it be a real external entity? This leads to the conclusion that imaginary movement is purely mental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحركة الوهمية وهمية بلا شبهة لاستحالة قيام الموجود بالموهوم. ولأنها أعني هذه الإمكانات القابلة للزيادة والنقصان تنفرض في الأعدام الصرفة. فإن ما بين يوم الطوفان ومحمد ﷺ أكثر مما بين بعثة موسى وبعثة محمد عليهما السلام. ولا شك أنَّ ما يمكن عروضه لأمور معدومة لا يكون موجوداً خارجياً. ثم التحقيق أن الحركة بمعنى القطع والزمان الذي هو مقدارها لا وجود لهما في الخارج، بل هما إنما يرتسمان في الخيال. لكن ليس ارتسامهما فيه من أمر معدوم بالضرورة، بل من أمرين موجودين في الخارج. لأنا نعلم أنَّ ذلك الامتداد المرتسم في الخيال بحيث لو فرض وجوده في الخارج وفرض فيه أجزاء لامتنع اجتماعها معاً، بل كان بعضها متقدماً على بعض، ولا يكون الامتداد العقلي كذلك إلا إذا كان في الخارج شيء مستمر غير مستقر يحصل في العقل بحسب استمراره وعدم استقراره ذلك الامتداد.
The imaginary movement is imaginary without doubt because it is impossible for an existent to subsist in an imaginary. And because these possibilities that are capable of increase and decrease are assumed in pure non-existents. For what is between the day of the Flood and Muhammad ﷺ is more than what is between the mission of Moses and the mission of Muhammad, peace be upon them. And there is no doubt that what can be attributed to non-existent things is not externally existent. Then the investigation is that movement in the sense of cutting and time which is its measure have no existence in the external world; rather they are only imprinted in the imagination. But their imprinting is not from a non-existent thing necessarily, but from two existing things in the external world. For we know that that extension imprinted in the imagination, such that if its existence were supposed in the external world and parts were supposed in it, their simultaneous coexistence would be impossible; rather some of them would be prior to others. And the mental extension would not be like that unless there were in the external world something continuous and unstable, by virtue of whose continuity and instability that extension occurs in the mind.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the mutakallimun's argument that time and movement have no external reality. It begins by asserting that 'imaginary movement' is indeed imaginary because an existing thing cannot subsist in what is merely imaginary. Then it notes that the 'possibilities' (al-imkanat) that differ in quantity (like the duration between historical events) are attributed to pure non-existents, so they cannot be externally real. The proof then states that movement (in the sense of traversing distance) and time (its measure) do not exist outside the mind; they are only imprints in the imagination. However, these imprints are not derived from nothing—they come from two external realities (namely, the continuous motion of an object and something else, like the flow of water). The reasoning is that if we imagine an extension with parts that cannot coexist (i.e., sequential parts), that requires something in the external world that is continuous and unstable (like motion) to cause that mental extension. Thus, time is mentally constructed but based on real motion.

Key Terms
الحركة الوهمية
الأعدام الصرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imaginary movement is completely unreal and has no basis.
Correction: The passage only denies its external existence, not its conceptual reality; it is used to show that such movement is mental, not a real entity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what proves that imaginary movement is not externally existent?
A) It is impossible for an existent to subsist in an imaginary thing.
B) The duration between prophets is measurable.
C) Movement is a property of bodies.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Imaginary movement is not externally existent because it can be attributed to pure non-existents like past historical intervals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you give emotional weight to imaginary timelines—like regrets about the past or anxieties about the future—as if they are real objects? What would change if you truly internalized that these intervals are purely non-existent?
?
When you find yourself measuring or comparing durations (e.g., 'I've waited so long for this'), which is more real to you: the external moment or the imagined interval between? How does this lesson expose the confusion?
?
Imagine someone says to you, 'My years of suffering are definitely real.' How would you respond using the argument of this passage—without dismissing their pain—to show that the duration itself is not externally existent? What does that mean for how you view your own trials?

Time and Movement Are Mental Constructs from External Motion
Affirms mental reality of time based on external motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mutakallimun's position that time and movement have no external existence but are mental imprints derived from two external realities, particularly continuous motion.

Core Idea
Time exists in the mind, grounded in external motion.

This lesson continues from the previous one. After establishing that imaginary movement is not externally real, the author now clarifies that time and movement are not completely unreal—they are imprints in the imagination that come from two existing things in the external world. The key is that continuous motion in the external world causes the mental extension we call time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the shift from negation to positive explanation.
Pay attention to 'ثم التحقيق' which signals a deeper investigation.
2
Understand the denial and affirmation
The passage states movement (in the sense of traversing distance) and time have no external existence. But they are imprinted in the imagination, and this imprinting is from two existing things in the external world.
The author avoids saying they are purely illusory.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The author argues that the mental extension (time) has parts that cannot coexist; if it were external, its parts would have to be simultaneous or sequential. Since they are sequential, there must be something continuous and unstable in the external world (like motion) to produce this mental extension.
This shows that time is a mental construct based on real motion.

Commentary
This passage presents the mutakallimun's argument that time and movement have no external reality. It begins by asserting that 'imaginary movement' is indeed imaginary because an existing thing cannot subsist in what is merely imaginary. Misconception: The mutakallimun deny time completely and consider it an illusion.
Correction: They deny its independent external existence but affirm its mental reality derived from real motion in the external world.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what causes the mental extension we call time?
A) A purely imaginary construct with no basis in reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You treat time as if it were a container that runs out. But this lesson says time is only a mental measure of your actions. If that is true, are you living as though your actions are the real substance, or are you enslaved to a mental construct? What would it look like to act today with the awareness that each moment is defined by what you do, not by how much 'time' you have left?
?
The author says time is imprinted from continuous, unstable motion. Your life is a sequence of such motions—breathing, thinking, moving. If time is merely your mind's way of grasping that flux, then your perception of 'wasting time' might actually be a failure to align your actions with what matters. What is one unstable, continuous action you engage in daily that you could reframe as the very substance of your existence, rather than something you 'spend time' on?
?
If time has no external reality, then your anxiety about the future or regret about the past is based on a mental construct, not on something that exists outside your mind. How would your relationship with your past mistakes and future plans change if you truly internalized that only the present motion of your soul—your current intention and action—is real? Can you identify one past regret or future fear and consciously relegate it to the imagination, focusing instead on a concrete action you can take now?

What Is Kalam?
beginner
5 min
Time as the Substrate of Priority and Posteriority
Al-Jurjani defines time as the essential substrate of priority and posteriority, then answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that time is defined as the essential substrate of priority and posteriority, and that even if priority and posteriority are mental considerations, they necessitate a real entity that grounds them—namely, time.

Core Idea
Time is the real foundation for the mental relations of priority and posteriority.

How do we define time? Theologians and philosophers have debated whether time is a real entity or a mere mental construct. Al-Jurjani offers a precise definition: time is the thing whose parts are essentially arranged as prior and posterior. He then addresses the objection that priority and posteriority are only mental considerations, showing that even mental relations require a real substrate. This passage establishes time as a real entity grounded in the order of parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
First, read the Arabic text carefully. Notice how Al-Jurjani presents his definition in a compact, logical style.
The phrase 'لذاته' (essentially) is crucial.
2
Identify the definition of time
Find the sentence where time is defined. What does Al-Jurjani mean by 'that thing whose part is essentially before a part...'?
The definition emphasizes that time has parts that are intrinsically ordered.
3
Understand the objection and response
The passage ends with a response to the claim that priority and posteriority are merely mental considerations. How does Al-Jurjani answer? Does he deny the claim or accept it?
He seems to accept that they are mental, but argues that time is still needed as a real basis.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about why this matters: if time is a real entity with essential ordering, it plays a crucial role in arguments about creation and change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتلخيصه أي تلخيص الوجه الثاني وتحريره إن هاهنا مفهومهما بلا اعتبار أمر آخر معهما لم يكن ثمة تقدم ولا تأخر فذلك الأمر الذي لحقه التقدم والتأخر لذاته هو الذي نسميه بالزمان إذ لا نعني بالزمان إلا الأمر الذي يكون جزء منه لذاته قبل جزء وجزء منه لذاته بعد جزء على معنى أن الجزء الموصوف منه بالقبلية يمتنع يتصف بالبعدية والموصوف منه بالبعدية يمتنع أن يتصف بالقبلية والجواب لا عن الوجه الثاني أن ذلك ذكرتموه أعني القبلية والبعدية اعتبار عقلي
And its summary, i.e., the summary and reformulation of the second aspect: that here if their two concepts are taken without considering any other thing with them, there is no priority or posteriority. So that thing which is affected by priority and posteriority essentially is what we call time. For we do not mean by time except that thing whose part is essentially before a part and whose part is essentially after a part, in the sense that the part described by priority cannot be described by posteriority, and the part described by posteriority cannot be described by priority. And the answer, not concerning the second aspect, that what you mentioned, i.e., priority and posteriority, is a mental consideration.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage first provides a definition of time (زمان) as a summary of the second argument. Al-Jurjani explains that if we consider the concepts of priority and posteriority alone without any additional entity, no actual priority or posteriority exists. Therefore, there must be a thing that is essentially characterized by priority and posteriority, and that thing is time. He defines time precisely: it is an entity such that one part is essentially prior to another part, and another part is essentially posterior, and a part described by priority cannot be described by posteriority, and vice versa. This establishes time as a real entity with intrinsic order. The passage then presents a response to an objection (the second aspect) that claims priority and posteriority are merely mental considerations (اعتبار عقلي). The answer seems to accept this characterization, stating that what is mentioned—priority and posteriority—is indeed a mental consideration. However, this does not negate the need for time, because even if these relations are mental, they still require a real substrate that grounds the ordering, which is time. The argument does not rely on the external existence of these relations but on their conceptual necessity.

Key Terms
زمان
تقدم
تأخر
جزء
لذاته
اعتبار عقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if priority and posteriority are mental considerations, then time is not needed.
Correction: The passage clarifies that mental considerations still require a real substrate, which is time. The mental status of relations does not eliminate the need for a real entity that grounds them.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about priority and posteriority in relation to time?
A) They are identical to time
B) They are real external attributes that define time
C) They are mental considerations, but time is the real substrate that grounds them
D) They are irrelevant to the definition of time

Key Takeaway
Time is the real entity whose parts are intrinsically ordered as prior and posterior, providing the necessary substrate even if the relations themselves are mental considerations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the priorities and delays in your daily life, do you view them as mere mental labels, or as reflections of a real order set by Allah? How does this passage challenge you to see time as a divinely created substrate that gives weight to your choices?
?
If time has an intrinsic order where a prior moment can never become posterior, what does that mean for your understanding of repentance? Can you truly 'go back' and undo the past, or does the reality of time emphasize the permanence of actions and the urgency of seeking forgiveness now?
?
The passage describes time as something whose parts cannot be both prior and posterior. In your spiritual journey, are there areas where you try to be both—wanting the priority of devotion and the freedom of the world? How can you align yourself with the natural order of time by establishing clear priorities that honor Allah?

What Is Kalam?
intermediate
6 min
Defining Time: The Real Substrate of Priority and Posteriority
Al-Jurjani defines time and its essential characteristics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Jurjani defines time as a real extension that is essentially characterized by priority and posteriority, and why this definition is necessary for kalam.

Core Idea
Time is the real extension whose parts are inherently prior or posterior.

Al-Jurjani begins by establishing what time is: not a mere mental construct, but a real entity that serves as the ultimate substrate for priority and posteriority. This definition underpins the entire debate about time's reality. As you read, notice how he carefully distinguishes between something that merely borrows priority and something that has it essentially.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on definition
Read the Arabic passage from 'المرصد الثاني' through 'يمتنع أن يتصف بالقبلية' and its translation. Focus on how al-Jurjani describes the matter that is essentially prior and posterior.
2
Identify the key terms
Spot the terms الزمان, القبلية, البعدية, and الامتداد. Understand that الزمان is defined as an extension (امتداد) whose parts are inherently ordered.
3
Understand the essentiality condition
Note that al-Jurjani insists that the part described by priority cannot be described by posteriority, and vice versa. This means the parts have these attributes by their very nature.
This contrasts with accidental priority, like Zayd being prior to 'Amr in birth.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Ask yourself: Why does al-Jurjani need to define time this way? This definition sets up the refutation of those who say priority and posteriority are merely mental considerations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد السابع: إنكار المتكلمين للزمن وتلخيصه أي تلخيص الوجه الثاني وتحريره إن هاهنا مفهومهما بلا اعتبار أمر آخر معهما لم يكن ثمة تقدم ولا تأخر فذلك الأمر الذي لحقه التقدم والتأخر لذاته هو الذي نسميه بالزمان إذ لا نعني بالزمان إلا الأمر الذي يكون جزء منه لذاته قبل جزء وجزء منه لذاته بعد جزء على معنى أن الجزء الموصوف منه بالقبلية يمتنع أن يتصف بالبعدية والموصوف منه بالبعدية يمتنع أن يتصف بالقبلية والجواب لا عن الوجه الثاني أن ذلك ذكرتموه أعني القبلية والبعدية اعتبار عقلي أن يصير واسطة في اتصافهما بهما وإن كان موصوفاً بهما بواسطة شيء آخر موصوف بهما بواسطة شيء آخر وهلم جرا يلزم التسلسل في موصوفات القبلية والبعدية فاندفع ما قيل: أن أريد بقوله: ليس لذاتيهما انتفاء الواسطة في العروض فلا نسلم الملازمة المستفادة من قوله: وإلا لامتنع انفكاكهما عنها فإن الحركة مع الجسم لا واسطة بينهما في العروض مع جواز الانفكاك بينهما وإن أريد انتفاء الواسطة في الثبوت فلا نسلم قوله فلا بد من شيء آخر يتصف بهما لذاته إذ لا بد من وجود شيء يكون واسطة في ثبوتهما لهما لاتصاف ذلك الشيء بهما فضلاً عن أن يكون لذاته. قوله: (هو الذي نسميه بالزمان وهو موجود لأنه لا بد في الخارج من أمر مقارن للأب والابن بحيث إذا لاحظ الوهم وقسمه إلى جزأين يحكم بامتناع اجتماعهما وأن أحدهما مثل الآخر، وإن لم تكن القبلية والبعدية ولا الاتصاف بهما في الخارج ولظهور هذه المقدمة لم يتعرض لها. قوله: (والجواب إلخ) هذا الجواب مندفع بالتقرير الذي ذكرناه إذ لا استدلال بوجود القبلية والبعدية حتى يقال: إنهما اعتباريان بل باتصاف الأشياء بهما في الذهن كما عرفت. عليه بقوله: لأن التقدم أمر إضافي إذ لا امتناع في كون غير الإضافي سبباً للإضافي بل من قوله: فالقبلية والبعدية مما يختلف به العدم المعتبر معه فإنه فهم منه على توجيه الشارح انفكاك التقدم من الأب والتأخر من الابن، ولو كانا منشأين للتقدم والتأخر لامتناع انفكاكهما عنهما بقي فيه بحث وهو أنه لا يلزم من عدم كونهما منشأين لهما وجود شيء آخر يتصف بهما لذاته. ألا الجسم ليس منشأ للحركة العارضة له، یری أنه ليس هناك شيء مغاير للجسم يتصف مع بالحركة حقيقة إن قلت: المراد من قوله: ليس لذاتيهما إن ذاتيهما ليسا معروضين حقيقيين لهما يصح قوله: فلا بد من شيء آخر يتصف بهما لذاته: قلت الدليل الذي ذكره أعني وإلا امتنع انفكاكهما عنهما لا يفيد ذلك لأن مجرد كون شيء معروضاً حقيقياً لشيء لا يستلزم امتناع انفكاك أحدهما عن الآخر فاعتبر الحركة والجسم وغاية ما يتكلف أن يقال: إنه لما يبين أن عروض القبلية والبعدية للأب والابن ليس منشؤه ذاتيهما فلا بد له منشأ حقيقي بالضرورة ولما علم ضرورة أن منشأه المنشأ الحقيقي له أعني الامتداد الذي لا يقبل لذاته الاجتماع بل بعض أجزائه مقدم وبعضه مؤخر لذاته كما ينبه عليه انقطاع سؤال وجه تقدم ولادة زيد على ولاده عمرو وإذا انتهى الجواب إلى أن ولادة زيد في سنة ثمانين وولادة عمرو في سنة تسعين على ما سبق في مباحث الحدوث يكون جزؤه المقدم ظرفاً للأب وجزؤه المؤخر ظرفاً للابن أقام قوله: فلا بد من شيء آخر يتصف بهما لذاته مقام فلا بد من شيء آخر يكون منشأ لهما لذاته لأنه هو الدال على وجود الزمان بزعمهم فتأمل واعلم أن اللازم من الدليل على تقدير تمامه زيادة القبلية على الأمور المذكورة وأما وجودها فلم يتعرض له في الاستدلال حتى يثبت وجود معروضه، أعني الزمان والمسطور في كتب القوم بعد الاستدلال على زيادتها بما ذكر أنها وجودية لأنها نقيض اللاقبلية كما مر مثله مراراً، فتقرير المصنف قاصر. قوله: (فإن عدم الحادث مقدم على وجوده قطعاً) فيكون التقدم عارضاً للعدم وصفة له (وما يعرض للعدم ويكون صفة له لا يكون أمراً موجوداً محققاً في الخارج) بل يكون أمراً موهوماً اعتبارياً فلا يستدعي محلاً موجوداً فلا يلزم أن يكون معروض القبلية بالذات موجوداً خارجياً كما ادعيتموه. قوله: (فإن عدم إلخ) سند للمنع المستفاد من المقدمة الثانية أي لا نسلم أن القبلية والبعدية موجودتان حتى يلزم وجود موصوفهما فإن عدم الحادث موصوف بالقبلية وليست موجودة وقد ظهر لك مما سبق أن السند لا يصلح للسندية لأن عدم الحادث ليس موصوفاً بها حقيقة وإن كان مقارناً لها.
The second observation – the seventh topic: The denial of time by the mutakallimun. And its summary, i.e., the summary of the second aspect and its refinement: That here, the two concepts (priority and posteriority) without considering another matter with them, there would be no priority or posteriority. So that matter which is characterized by priority and posteriority essentially is what we call time, for we mean by time nothing but the matter of which a part is essentially before a part and a part is essentially after a part, in the sense that the part described by priority cannot be described by posteriority, and the part described by posteriority cannot be described by priority. And the answer, not from the second aspect, is that what you mentioned, namely priority and posteriority, is a mental consideration. That [the priority and posteriority] become a medium in their characterization by them, and if they were characterized by them through another thing characterized by them through another thing, and so on, an infinite regress in the things characterized by priority and posteriority would follow. So what was said is repelled: If by his statement 'not essentially' he meant the negation of the medium in inherence, we do not grant the implication derived from his statement 'otherwise they would be inseparable from them', for motion and body have no medium between them in inherence, yet separation between them is possible. And if he meant the negation of the medium in subsistence, we do not grant his statement 'so there must be another thing characterized by them essentially', for there must exist a thing that is a medium in their subsistence for them, for that thing to be characterized by them, let alone that it be essential. His statement: 'It is what we call time, and it exists, because in the external world there must be something concomitant to the father and son, such that when the estimative faculty observes it and divides it into two parts, it judges that they cannot both exist together and that one of them is like the other, even if priority and posteriority and the characterization by them are not in the external world, and because this premise is evident, it was not discussed.' His statement: 'And the answer etc.' This answer is refuted by the exposition we mentioned, for there is no inference from the existence of priority and posteriority such that it is said they are mental, but rather from the characterization of things by them in the mind as you have known. Against him by his statement: 'Because priority is an additive thing', for there is no impossibility in something non-additive being a cause of an additive. Rather, from his statement: 'So priority and posteriority are something by which the non-being considered with it differs', for it was understood from it, according to the commentator's interpretation, the separation of priority from the father and posteriority from the son. And if they were origins for priority and posteriority, their separation from them would be impossible. There remains a discussion: it is not necessary that because they are not origins for them, there exists another thing characterized by them essentially. For example, the body is not an origin for the motion that inheres in it; there is no thing other than the body that is truly characterized by motion. If you say: What is meant by his statement 'not essentially' is that their essences are not true substrates for them, so his statement 'so there must be another thing characterized by them essentially' is valid. I say: The proof he mentioned, namely 'otherwise they would be inseparable from them', does not yield that, because the mere fact that a thing is a true substrate for something does not entail the impossibility of one being separated from the other – consider motion and body. The utmost that can be said is that since it is shown that the inherence of priority and posteriority in the father and son does not originate from their essences, there must necessarily be a true origin for them. And since it is known necessarily that its true origin is the extension which essentially does not admit combination, but some of its parts are prior and some posterior essentially, as indicated by the cessation of the question about the priority of Zayd's birth over 'Amr's birth. When the answer concludes that Zayd's birth in the year eighty and 'Amr's birth in the year ninety, as previously in the discussions of temporal origination, its prior part is the container for the father and its posterior part is the container for the son, he substituted his statement 'so there must be another thing characterized by them essentially' for 'so there must be another thing that is an origin for them essentially', because it is what indicates the existence of time according to their claim. So reflect. And know that what is necessary from the proof, assuming its completeness, is the addition of priority to the mentioned matters; as for its existence, it was not addressed in the inference such that the existence of its substrate, i.e., time, is established. What is recorded in the books of the folk after inference to its addition as mentioned is that it is existent because it is the opposite of non-priority, as similar has passed many times. So the author's exposition is deficient. His statement: 'For the non-being of the originated event is prior to its existence, definitely' – so priority becomes an accident of non-being and a quality of it, 'and what occurs to non-being and is a quality of it cannot be an existing realized thing in the external world' – rather it is an illusory mental thing, so it does not demand an existing locus; so it does not follow that the substrate of priority essentially is an external existent as you claimed. His statement: 'For non-being etc.' is a support for the denial derived from the second premise, i.e., we do not grant that priority and posteriority exist such that the existence of their characterized thing follows, for the non-being of the originated event is characterized by priority and it does not exist. And it has become clear to you from the above that the support is not suitable for support because the non-being of the originated event is not truly characterized by them, even though it is concomitant with them.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is a passage from al-Jurjani's commentary on al-Iji's Mawaqif, addressing the seventh topic: the denial of time by the mutakallimun. The argument here is a response to those who claim that priority and posteriority are merely mental considerations, and that time is not a real entity. The commentary first defines time as that which is essentially characterized by priority and posteriority – a single extended reality whose parts are inherently prior or posterior, such that a prior part cannot be posterior and vice versa. The opponent objects that priority and posteriority are mental considerations, not real. The commentator refutes this by showing that if priority and posteriority were merely mental, then objects would need an infinite chain of intermediaries to be characterized by them, which is absurd. Instead, there must be a real entity (time) that is the direct substrate of these relations. The objection that non-being can be characterized by priority is answered: non-being is not truly characterized by priority; rather, priority is a real attribute inhering in time, which is a real extention. The commentator also addresses the issue of whether the proof establishes the existence of time or merely its addition as a concept. He notes that the proof aims to show both, but the author's exposition is deficient in this regard.

Key Terms
الزمان
القبلية
البعدية
الامتداد
لذاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is merely a mental construct or a measure of motion.
Correction: Al-Jurjani argues that time is a real extension whose parts are inherently prior and posterior, not a subjective concept.

Checkpoint
According to al-Jurjani's definition, what is the characteristic of a part of time that is described as prior?
A) It can also be described as posterior.
B) It cannot be described as posterior.
C) It is a measure of motion.
D) It is a mental consideration.

Key Takeaway
Time is defined as a real extension whose parts are inherently prior and posterior, grounding the objective reality of temporal relations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that time is a real extension with parts that are fixed in priority and posteriority. How does this truth affect your view of your past sins? Do you treat them as real and unchangeable, or do you minimize them? What would it mean for you to truly accept that each moment of your past is eternally recorded in this real order?
?
If time is not just a mental construct but a created reality, then every second is a gift from Allah with its own fixed place. Are you living each moment as if it matters eternally, or do you waste time as if it were merely subjective? What one change can you make today to honor the reality of time?
?
Al-Jurjani argues that priority and posteriority would not exist without a real substrate. Your life unfolds in a real sequence that cannot be reversed. Does this thought fill you with hope or fear? Will you use the present moment—the only part of time you can act in—to prepare for the fixed future that awaits you?

What Is Kalam?
advanced
8 min
Refuting the Mental Consideration Objection
Al-Jurjani refutes the mental-consideration objection using infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why priority and posteriority cannot be merely mental considerations, and how the infinite regress argument proves the existence of a real substrate (time).

Core Idea
If priority and posteriority were mental, characterization would require an infinite regress.

Al-Jurjani now addresses the key objection: that priority and posteriority are merely mental considerations. He uses a powerful argument: if they were purely mental, then for something to be characterized by them, it would need another thing that is also characterized, leading to an infinite regress. This regress is impossible, so there must be a real entity (time) that is the direct substrate. Pay attention to how he handles the counterexamples about motion and non-being.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first refutation
Read from 'والجواب لا عن الوجه الثاني' to 'فلا بد من شيء آخر يتصف بهما لذاته' and the translation. Notice how al-Jurjani sets up the infinite regress.
The opponent says priority/posteriority are mental considerations ('اعتبار عقلي').
2
Understand the infinite regress argument
Al-Jurjani argues that if they are mental, then for something to be characterized by them, it would need another thing that is also characterized, and so on, leading to an infinite regress. This is absurd, so there must be something characterized essentially.
The regress is in the 'things characterized' (موصوفات), not in the attributes themselves.
3
Examine the counterexample of motion and body
The opponent might object that motion and body have no medium in inherence yet can separate. Al-Jurjani addresses this by distinguishing between inherence and subsistence.
He says: if 'not essentially' means no medium in inherence, we don't grant the implication. If it means no medium in subsistence, we deny the conclusion.
4
Consider the objection from non-being
Later, the objection that non-being (عدم الحادث) is prior to existence is raised. Al-Jurjani responds that non-being is not truly characterized by priority; it is merely concomitant.
This shows priority is a real attribute that requires a real substrate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد السابع: إنكار المتكلمين للزمن وتلخيصه أي تلخيص الوجه الثاني وتحريره إن هاهنا مفهومهما بلا اعتبار أمر آخر معهما لم يكن ثمة تقدم ولا تأخر فذلك الأمر الذي لحقه التقدم والتأخر لذاته هو الذي نسميه بالزمان إذ لا نعني بالزمان إلا الأمر الذي يكون جزء منه لذاته قبل جزء وجزء منه لذاته بعد جزء على معنى أن الجزء الموصوف منه بالقبلية يمتنع أن يتصف بالبعدية والموصوف منه بالبعدية يمتنع أن يتصف بالقبلية والجواب لا عن الوجه الثاني أن ذلك ذكرتموه أعني القبلية والبعدية اعتبار عقلي أن يصير واسطة في اتصافهما بهما وإن كان موصوفاً بهما بواسطة شيء آخر موصوف بهما بواسطة شيء آخر وهلم جرا يلزم التسلسل في موصوفات القبلية والبعدية فاندفع ما قيل: أن أريد بقوله: ليس لذاتيهما انتفاء الواسطة في العروض فلا نسلم الملازمة المستفادة من قوله: وإلا لامتنع انفكاكهما عنها فإن الحركة مع الجسم لا واسطة بينهما في العروض مع جواز الانفكاك بينهما وإن أريد انتفاء الواسطة في الثبوت فلا نسلم قوله فلا بد من شيء آخر يتصف بهما لذاته إذ لا بد من وجود شيء يكون واسطة في ثبوتهما لهما لاتصاف ذلك الشيء بهما فضلاً عن أن يكون لذاته. قوله: (هو الذي نسميه بالزمان وهو موجود لأنه لا بد في الخارج من أمر مقارن للأب والابن بحيث إذا لاحظ الوهم وقسمه إلى جزأين يحكم بامتناع اجتماعهما وأن أحدهما مثل الآخر، وإن لم تكن القبلية والبعدية ولا الاتصاف بهما في الخارج ولظهور هذه المقدمة لم يتعرض لها. قوله: (والجواب إلخ) هذا الجواب مندفع بالتقرير الذي ذكرناه إذ لا استدلال بوجود القبلية والبعدية حتى يقال: إنهما اعتباريان بل باتصاف الأشياء بهما في الذهن كما عرفت. عليه بقوله: لأن التقدم أمر إضافي إذ لا امتناع في كون غير الإضافي سبباً للإضافي بل من قوله: فالقبلية والبعدية مما يختلف به العدم المعتبر معه فإنه فهم منه على توجيه الشارح انفكاك التقدم من الأب والتأخر من الابن، ولو كانا منشأين للتقدم والتأخر لامتناع انفكاكهما عنهما بقي فيه بحث وهو أنه لا يلزم من عدم كونهما منشأين لهما وجود شيء آخر يتصف بهما لذاته. ألا الجسم ليس منشأ للحركة العارضة له، یری أنه ليس هناك شيء مغاير للجسم يتصف مع بالحركة حقيقة إن قلت: المراد من قوله: ليس لذاتيهما إن ذاتيهما ليسا معروضين حقيقيين لهما يصح قوله: فلا بد من شيء آخر يتصف بهما لذاته: قلت الدليل الذي ذكره أعني وإلا امتنع انفكاكهما عنهما لا يفيد ذلك لأن مجرد كون شيء معروضاً حقيقياً لشيء لا يستلزم امتناع انفكاك أحدهما عن الآخر فاعتبر الحركة والجسم وغاية ما يتكلف أن يقال: إنه لما يبين أن عروض القبلية والبعدية للأب والابن ليس منشؤه ذاتيهما فلا بد له منشأ حقيقي بالضرورة ولما علم ضرورة أن منشأه المنشأ الحقيقي له أعني الامتداد الذي لا يقبل لذاته الاجتماع بل بعض أجزائه مقدم وبعضه مؤخر لذاته كما ينبه عليه انقطاع سؤال وجه تقدم ولادة زيد على ولاده عمرو وإذا انتهى الجواب إلى أن ولادة زيد في سنة ثمانين وولادة عمرو في سنة تسعين على ما سبق في مباحث الحدوث يكون جزؤه المقدم ظرفاً للأب وجزؤه المؤخر ظرفاً للابن أقام قوله: فلا بد من شيء آخر يتصف بهما لذاته مقام فلا بد من شيء آخر يكون منشأ لهما لذاته لأنه هو الدال على وجود الزمان بزعمهم فتأمل واعلم أن اللازم من الدليل على تقدير تمامه زيادة القبلية على الأمور المذكورة وأما وجودها فلم يتعرض له في الاستدلال حتى يثبت وجود معروضه، أعني الزمان والمسطور في كتب القوم بعد الاستدلال على زيادتها بما ذكر أنها وجودية لأنها نقيض اللاقبلية كما مر مثله مراراً، فتقرير المصنف قاصر. قوله: (فإن عدم الحادث مقدم على وجوده قطعاً) فيكون التقدم عارضاً للعدم وصفة له (وما يعرض للعدم ويكون صفة له لا يكون أمراً موجوداً محققاً في الخارج) بل يكون أمراً موهوماً اعتبارياً فلا يستدعي محلاً موجوداً فلا يلزم أن يكون معروض القبلية بالذات موجوداً خارجياً كما ادعيتموه. قوله: (فإن عدم إلخ) سند للمنع المستفاد من المقدمة الثانية أي لا نسلم أن القبلية والبعدية موجودتان حتى يلزم وجود موصوفهما فإن عدم الحادث موصوف بالقبلية وليست موجودة وقد ظهر لك مما سبق أن السند لا يصلح للسندية لأن عدم الحادث ليس موصوفاً بها حقيقة وإن كان مقارناً لها.
The second observation – the seventh topic: The denial of time by the mutakallimun. And its summary, i.e., the summary of the second aspect and its refinement: That here, the two concepts (priority and posteriority) without considering another matter with them, there would be no priority or posteriority. So that matter which is characterized by priority and posteriority essentially is what we call time, for we mean by time nothing but the matter of which a part is essentially before a part and a part is essentially after a part, in the sense that the part described by priority cannot be described by posteriority, and the part described by posteriority cannot be described by priority. And the answer, not from the second aspect, is that what you mentioned, namely priority and posteriority, is a mental consideration. That [the priority and posteriority] become a medium in their characterization by them, and if they were characterized by them through another thing characterized by them through another thing, and so on, an infinite regress in the things characterized by priority and posteriority would follow. So what was said is repelled: If by his statement 'not essentially' he meant the negation of the medium in inherence, we do not grant the implication derived from his statement 'otherwise they would be inseparable from them', for motion and body have no medium between them in inherence, yet separation between them is possible. And if he meant the negation of the medium in subsistence, we do not grant his statement 'so there must be another thing characterized by them essentially', for there must exist a thing that is a medium in their subsistence for them, for that thing to be characterized by them, let alone that it be essential. His statement: 'It is what we call time, and it exists, because in the external world there must be something concomitant to the father and son, such that when the estimative faculty observes it and divides it into two parts, it judges that they cannot both exist together and that one of them is like the other, even if priority and posteriority and the characterization by them are not in the external world, and because this premise is evident, it was not discussed.' His statement: 'And the answer etc.' This answer is refuted by the exposition we mentioned, for there is no inference from the existence of priority and posteriority such that it is said they are mental, but rather from the characterization of things by them in the mind as you have known. Against him by his statement: 'Because priority is an additive thing', for there is no impossibility in something non-additive being a cause of an additive. Rather, from his statement: 'So priority and posteriority are something by which the non-being considered with it differs', for it was understood from it, according to the commentator's interpretation, the separation of priority from the father and posteriority from the son. And if they were origins for priority and posteriority, their separation from them would be impossible. There remains a discussion: it is not necessary that because they are not origins for them, there exists another thing characterized by them essentially. For example, the body is not an origin for the motion that inheres in it; there is no thing other than the body that is truly characterized by motion. If you say: What is meant by his statement 'not essentially' is that their essences are not true substrates for them, so his statement 'so there must be another thing characterized by them essentially' is valid. I say: The proof he mentioned, namely 'otherwise they would be inseparable from them', does not yield that, because the mere fact that a thing is a true substrate for something does not entail the impossibility of one being separated from the other – consider motion and body. The utmost that can be said is that since it is shown that the inherence of priority and posteriority in the father and son does not originate from their essences, there must necessarily be a true origin for them. And since it is known necessarily that its true origin is the extension which essentially does not admit combination, but some of its parts are prior and some posterior essentially, as indicated by the cessation of the question about the priority of Zayd's birth over 'Amr's birth. When the answer concludes that Zayd's birth in the year eighty and 'Amr's birth in the year ninety, as previously in the discussions of temporal origination, its prior part is the container for the father and its posterior part is the container for the son, he substituted his statement 'so there must be another thing characterized by them essentially' for 'so there must be another thing that is an origin for them essentially', because it is what indicates the existence of time according to their claim. So reflect. And know that what is necessary from the proof, assuming its completeness, is the addition of priority to the mentioned matters; as for its existence, it was not addressed in the inference such that the existence of its substrate, i.e., time, is established. What is recorded in the books of the folk after inference to its addition as mentioned is that it is existent because it is the opposite of non-priority, as similar has passed many times. So the author's exposition is deficient. His statement: 'For the non-being of the originated event is prior to its existence, definitely' – so priority becomes an accident of non-being and a quality of it, 'and what occurs to non-being and is a quality of it cannot be an existing realized thing in the external world' – rather it is an illusory mental thing, so it does not demand an existing locus; so it does not follow that the substrate of priority essentially is an external existent as you claimed. His statement: 'For non-being etc.' is a support for the denial derived from the second premise, i.e., we do not grant that priority and posteriority exist such that the existence of their characterized thing follows, for the non-being of the originated event is characterized by priority and it does not exist. And it has become clear to you from the above that the support is not suitable for support because the non-being of the originated event is not truly characterized by them, even though it is concomitant with them.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is a passage from al-Jurjani's commentary on al-Iji's Mawaqif, addressing the seventh topic: the denial of time by the mutakallimun. The argument here is a response to those who claim that priority and posteriority are merely mental considerations, and that time is not a real entity. The commentary first defines time as that which is essentially characterized by priority and posteriority – a single extended reality whose parts are inherently prior or posterior, such that a prior part cannot be posterior and vice versa. The opponent objects that priority and posteriority are mental considerations, not real. The commentator refutes this by showing that if priority and posteriority were merely mental, then objects would need an infinite chain of intermediaries to be characterized by them, which is absurd. Instead, there must be a real entity (time) that is the direct substrate of these relations. The objection that non-being can be characterized by priority is answered: non-being is not truly characterized by priority; rather, priority is a real attribute inhering in time, which is a real extention. The commentator also addresses the issue of whether the proof establishes the existence of time or merely its addition as a concept. He notes that the proof aims to show both, but the author's exposition is deficient in this regard.

Key Terms
اعتبار عقلي
التسلسل
العروض
الموصوف
العدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Priority and posteriority are purely subjective, so time is not real.
Correction: Al-Jurjani shows that if they were purely subjective, an infinite regress would result; therefore a real substrate (time) is necessary.

Checkpoint
According to al-Jurjani, what problem arises if priority and posteriority are merely mental considerations?
A) They would be contradictory.
B) They would lead to an infinite regress in the things characterized.
C) They would be inseparable from their subjects.
D) They would not exist at all.

Key Takeaway
The infinite regress argument demonstrates that priority and posteriority cannot be mere mental constructs; they require a real substratum, which is time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat time as a real constraint in your life—a deadline for accountability before Allah—or do you mentally push it aside, living as if priority and posteriority are just thoughts? What would change if you fully internalized that time is a real substratum that makes your actions real?
?
When you reflect on your own character, do you consider the 'priority' of your intentions and the 'posteriority' of your actions as mere mental labels, or do you see them as grounded in a real sequence that Allah will hold you to? How does that awareness affect your next decision?
?
The argument shows that denying the reality of priority leads to an infinite regress. In your life, are there areas where you avoid facing a fundamental priority (like repenting before death) by making endless intermediaries? What is one concrete step you can take today to cut that regress and submit to what is truly prior?

The First School on Time: Essential Priority and Posteriority
Al-Jurjani introduces the eighth topic on the reality of time and describes the first of five schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first school's definition of time as a thing essentially characterized by priority and posteriority, and how it differs from conventional notions and the excluded illusory view.

Core Idea
Time is a real entity with an inherent order of priority and posteriority.

Al-Jurjani begins the eighth topic on the reality of time by listing five schools. This lesson focuses on the first school, which defines time as a single thing whose parts are essentially prior and posterior. We'll also see why the view that time is purely illusory is excluded from this classification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Notice the definition of time as 'a thing which is characterized by priority and posteriority essentially'.
The passage also distinguishes this from conventional priority like father-son.
2
Identify the key distinction
Contrast 'essential priority and posteriority' with conventional uses. Ask yourself: what makes something essentially prior? The passage explains that it's a single thing that, when divided, has an irreversible order.
3
Understand the exclusion of the sixth school
The passage mentions a sixth school that considers time purely illusory. Why is it excluded? Because it does not belong to the five schools that assume time has some reality.
This highlights that the five schools all affirm some form of real time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثامن : حقيقة الزمان ( في حقيقة الزمان (وفيه أي في الزمان باعتبار تعين حقيقته (مذاهب ) خمسة شيئاً تلحقه القبلية والبعدية لذاته غير ما يقال له في العرف إنه متقدم ومتأخر كالأب قوله: ( في حقيقة الزمان أي في ماهيته الموجودة فالمذهب السادس الذي أشرنا إليه فيما سبق وهو أنه وهمي محض انتزعه الوهم من حصول الحركة بين الطرفين خارج عن المذكورة هاهنا والاحتمالات قوله: (تلحقه القبلية والبعدية لذاته بمعنى أن هاهنا شيئاً واحداً إذا قسمه الوهم إلى جزأين يحكم بأن أحدهما قبل الآخر لأجل ذاته بحيث يمتنع ما أن يصير هو قبل بعد وبالعكس
The eighth topic: The reality of time. (On the reality of time) – and in it, i.e., in time considered with respect to the determination of its reality, (there are five schools): a thing which is characterized by priority and posteriority essentially, other than what is conventionally called prior and posterior, like the father. His statement: 'On the reality of time' i.e., on its existing quiddity. So the sixth school, which we alluded to earlier, and it is that it is purely illusory, extracted by the estimative faculty from the occurrence of motion between two endpoints, is excluded from what is mentioned here and the possibilities. His statement: 'Is characterized by priority and posteriority essentially' means that here there is a single thing, when the estimative faculty divides it into two parts, it judges that one of them is before the other on account of its essence, such that it is impossible that the part which is before becomes after and vice versa.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage introduces the eighth topic on the reality of time. Al-Jurjani states that there are five schools (madhahib) regarding what time really is. He describes the first of these: time is a thing that is essentially characterized by priority and posteriority, distinct from conventional notions of 'prior' and 'posterior' like the father (who is called prior but is not essentially so). He explains that 'the reality of time' means its existing quiddity (mahiyya). He then notes that a sixth school, which holds time to be purely illusory (wahmi mahd) – derived by the estimative faculty from the occurrence of motion between two endpoints – is excluded from the present discussion. The central point is that according to the first school, time is a single real extension whose parts are inherently ordered as prior and posterior, so that when the mind divides it, it sees a necessary order that cannot be reversed.

Key Terms
حقيقة الزمان
القبلية
البعدية
الوهم
الماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the five schools include the view that time is purely illusory.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the sixth school (purely illusory) is excluded from the five schools mentioned here. The five schools all affirm some form of real time.

Checkpoint
How does the first school define time according to this passage?
A) As relative motion.
B) As a purely illusory concept.
C) As a thing essentially characterized by priority and posteriority.
D) As an accident inhering in bodies.

Key Takeaway
The first school holds that time is a real thing whose parts are essentially ordered as prior and posterior, a view distinct from both conventional priority and the purely illusory concept of time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time's parts are irreversibly ordered by essence, then your past moments are forever prior and cannot be made posterior. When you think of a sin you committed yesterday, does that fixity make you feel a greater urgency to repent now, before that moment becomes an eternal 'prior'? What specific action will you take today to ensure your 'prior' moments are filled with obedience?
?
You treat time as if it is a real continuum with an unchangeable order—but do you live as if each present moment is the only time you have to act? Consider the next hour: how will you use it differently knowing that this specific 'prior' moment in time is unique and will never return? Give one concrete intention.
?
The lesson distinguishes essential priority from conventional priority (like father and son). In your own life, do you sometimes treat the order of your priorities as merely conventional—reversible or relative—rather than as a fixed reality? What is one worldly priority you keep putting off as 'posterior' that, in truth, should be 'prior' in your relationship with Allah? Commit to reversing that order this week.

The Reality of Time: Five Schools and a Sixth View
Enumerates schools on time and notes a sixth rejected view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that scholars have proposed five main schools regarding the reality of time, and a sixth view that considers time as purely imaginary is rejected.

Core Idea
Time's reality is debated; five schools exist, and a sixth view treats it as imaginary.

This passage introduces the eighth topic of the discipline: the reality of time. The author states that there are five schools concerning time's essence, and then the commentator adds a sixth view that time is pure imagination extracted from motion. Understanding these positions is foundational for kalam discussions on time.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the English translation. Notice that the author immediately states there are five schools, but only the first is described here.
The passage is concise; take note of the term 'مذاهب خمسة' (five schools).
2
Identify the first school and the sixth
The first school says time is a thing that has priority and posteriority by itself, unlike conventional terms. The commentator then explains a sixth school—time as pure illusion—which falls outside the five.
The other four schools are not detailed in this passage.
3
Analyze the textual note
Notice the discussion about the pronoun in 'fihi' (therein) and the possible omitted genitive construction. This shows scholarly attention to precise wording.
This level of detail is common in kalam commentaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثامن : حقيقة الزمان. في حقيقة الزمان مذاهب خمسة: شيئاً تلحقه القبلية والبعدية لذاته غير ما يقال له في العرف إنه متقدم ومتأخر كالأب. قوله: (في حقيقة الزمان) أي في ماهيته الموجودة فالمذهب السادس الذي أشرنا إليه فيما سبق وهو أنه وهمي محض انتزعه الوهم من حصول الحركة بين الطرفين خارج عن المذكورة هاهنا والاحتمالات. الظاهر رجوعه إلى الحقيقة وفيه وجه آخر وهو أن يقال في قوله: حقيقة الزمان مضاف محذوف أي في بيان حقيقة الزمان وضمير فيه راجع إلى ذلك المضاف.
The eighth topic: The reality of time. Concerning the reality of time there are five schools: a thing to which priority and posteriority attach by essence, other than what is conventionally called prior and posterior like the father. His saying: ('concerning the reality of time') means concerning its existing quiddity. So the sixth school, which we referred to previously, is that it is pure imagination, which the imagination extracts from the occurrence of motion between two extremes, falling outside the mentioned ones here, and the possibilities. Apparently, the pronoun refers to the reality, and there is another aspect: that one says in his saying 'the reality of time' there is an omitted genitive construction, i.e., in the exposition of the reality of time, and the pronoun in it refers to that genitive.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage introduces the eighth topic: the reality of time (haqiqat al-zaman). The author states that there are five schools (madhahib) regarding time. The first school mentioned is that time is a thing that possesses priority (qabliyya) and posteriority (ba'diyya) by its essence, unlike ordinary things like a father which are called prior and posterior only in common parlance. Then the commentator explains that the sixth school, previously hinted at, is that time is pure illusion (wahm mahd) extracted by the imagination from the occurrence of motion between two extremes. This sixth school falls outside the five enumerated. The passage also includes a textual note about the phrase 'the reality of time': the pronoun in 'fihi' (therein) refers to the reality, and another interpretation suggests that there is a deleted idafa construction, meaning 'in the exposition of the reality of time'.

Key Terms
زمان
حقيقة
مذهب
وهم
حركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sixth school is considered a valid school alongside the five.
Correction: The author explicitly places the sixth school outside the five, implying it is not a sound view.

Checkpoint
How many schools are explicitly listed in the passage regarding the reality of time?
A) Five
B) Six
C) Seven
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The reality of time is debated among five main schools, with a sixth view (time as imaginary) usually rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You measure your life in days, hours, and minutes. If time is only a scaffolding sourced from motion—a product of imagination—what becomes of your anxiety over a past you cannot change or a future you cannot guarantee? Will you continue to let the clock rule your heart, or will you anchor your hope in the Eternal who transcends time?
?
The first school says time has priority and posteriority by essence. Your every sin and good deed is recorded in a temporal sequence. Before the Lord of all time, which moment of your life would you most fear to have brought forward and which would you most long to see accepted? How will you live today in light of that accounting?
?
You pray at appointed times, fast by the moon, and count years of zakat. Have these temporal markers become mere routines, or do they fracture your worldly illusions and draw you toward the Timeless? If the clock stopped forever right now, would your soul be ready to meet its Maker?

Essential vs. Conventional Priority and Posteriority
Commentary explains that priority and posteriority are not essential but arise from time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why priority and posteriority are not essential attributes of substances but arise from temporal relations.

Core Idea
Priority and posteriority belong to time, not to essence.

This passage clarifies a subtle distinction: while certain relations like causality are necessary, priority and posteriority (before/after) are not intrinsic to substances. The commentary uses the example of father and son to show that their substances are neutral to time; it is only the temporal context that makes one before the other.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the compact style of the commentary.
2
Identify the key example
The passage uses the father and son to illustrate conventional priority. Try to see why the father's substance is neutral before considering time.
3
Understand the logical argument
The passage argues that if priority were essential, it could never change. But we can imagine the son existing before the father, so it is not essential.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Priority and posteriority are annexed to time. The father is prior because he is in a prior time, not because his essence demands it.
5
Reflect on the distinction
Think about why this distinction matters in theology: it prevents attributing temporal properties to God's essence.

والابن وهو شيء لا يمكن أن يصير قبله بعد ولا بعده قبل لأن ما تقتضيه ذات الشيء يستحيل انفكاكه عنه ( وأما هذه الأشياء ( التي توصف في المتعارف بالقبلية والبعدية فيمكن فيها ذلك ( أعني أن يصير قبلها بعد وبعدها قبل ) لأنا لو فرضنا جوهر الأب من حيث هو جوهر لا يمتنع أن يوجد قبل ذلك ) أي قبل الابن ( ولا بعده بل نسبة ) جوهره إلى القبلية والبعدية على سواء وكذا الحال في جوهر الابن فإنه من حيث هو أن يوجد قبل الأب أو بعده ( فهذه الأشياء (إنما يلحقها التقدم والتأخر بسبب ذلك الأمر الذي تلحقه القبلية والبعدية لذاته ( فكان الأب متقدماً لكونه في زمان متقدم والابن متأخراً لكونه في زمان متأخر ولو لم يلاحظ ذلك ) أي لو لم يلاحظ وقوعهما في ذلك الأمر الذي هو معروض بالذات للقبلية والبعدية ( بل اعتبر الذاتان ) أعني : جوهري الأب والابن (من حيث أحدها لا أنَّ شيئاً واحداً يعرض له القبلية والبعدية لأجل ذاته حتى يرد أن شيئاً واحداً كيف يقتضي المتنافيين لذاته ولا أنَّ شيئاً واحداً يعرض له القبلية والبعدية باعتبار أجزائه في الخارج لأجل ذاته حتى يرد أنه يلزم أن يكون ذلك الشيء كماً منفصلاً وأن تجتمع أجزاؤه في الوجود
And the son, and it is a thing that cannot become before it after nor after it before, because what the essence of a thing necessitates is impossible to be separated from it. As for these things described conventionally as priority and posteriority, it is possible in them that (meaning: that what was before becomes after and what was after becomes before). For if we suppose the substance of the father insofar as it is substance, it is not impossible that it exist before that (i.e., before the son) nor after it; rather the relation of its substance to priority and posteriority is equal. And likewise the case in the substance of the son, for insofar as it is what it is, it can exist before the father or after him. So these things are only affected by priority and posteriority due to that thing which is the locus of priority and posteriority in itself. Thus the father was prior because he is in a prior time, and the son posterior because he is in a posterior time. And if that were not considered (i.e., if their occurrence in that thing which is the per se locus of priority and posteriority were not considered), but the two essences were considered (i.e., the substances of the father and son) in themselves, [then it is not that a single thing is affected by priority and posteriority in itself such that it would be objected how a single thing can necessitate two contradictories in itself, nor that a single thing is affected by priority and posteriority by consideration of its parts in the exterior in itself such that it would be objected that that thing would then have to be a discrete quantity and its parts would have to coexist in existence].
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the nature of priority and posteriority. It begins with an example: the son cannot change its essential order relative to the father because the essence of a thing necessitates something that cannot be separated. Then it distinguishes conventional priority/posteriority, which can change, from essential. For example, the substance of the father considered in itself does not require being before or after the son; it is neutral. So the father is called prior only because he exists in a prior time. If we consider only the essences, no single thing can have priority and posteriority essentially, nor can a thing have both by its parts, because that would require it to be a discrete quantity with coexisting parts.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Priority and posteriority are essential properties of things (e.g., father is inherently before son).
Correction: The passage shows that the substances themselves are neutral; priority comes from time.

Checkpoint
Why can the father and son be considered prior and posterior only in a conventional sense?
A) Because their essences necessitate priority.
B) Because priority and posteriority are not essential to their substances but come from time.
C) Because they are not real substances.
D) Because time is nothing.

Key Takeaway
Priority and posteriority are not essential to substances but are conventional, arising from temporal position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
